a father, and I will be able to call you Father. 

Please allow this time to be a good opportunity for us to weigh whether we have loved our father. Thus, they will have to shed tears centered around the stories of our father. 
Whenever I miss my husband, please help me to feel the heart of my father, who wished for the day of reunion between bride and groom centered on Jesus. And when the children miss their father, let them not forget that our father has come out after longing for his children for 6,000 years. Also, please help me realize that I exist today to sustain and rebuild history, and let me not forget that standing in this position without being able to embrace my sons and daughters and serve my husband is because I am the wife of an exile who has lost his country. Thus, let me know that I can only rest with my husband when I find that country, and that my daughters can grow up in infinite hope. 
In the Garden of Eden, there is a story of not being able to call you Father with the earnest heart of a beloved. Through this period, please allow your beloved daughters to be able to call you Father with a heart full of tears and to be able to touch and feel your deep heart. 
If there are tears flowing with a heart of gratitude that no one else possesses, and a heart of admiration that no one else possesses, those tears must become tears that can receive your comfort. Also, if there is a lonely appearance, please let your daughters stand in a position where you can come and provide comfort of mercy and compassion. If there are daughters who can be such wives and mothers, please be with them from the perspective of parents. Thus, I earnestly hope and wish that that place may become a place where we can comfort and be comforted. 
Now, the year 1970 is almost over. The year 1971 is approaching us, so we must once again think about how we will dedicate this new decade of the 70s to you. Therefore, we should welcome the 1970s with joy while reflecting on the sorrowful 1960s. However, before we are joyful, we must become a group of unification that struggles to dedicate that joy to you with a heart of filial piety. 
The time of joy has come, and we should not adorn ourselves and elevate ourselves, but rather adorn your nation and your world and adorn you, forgetting our own fatigue, saying that this is the wish I have longed for, and become devoted sons and daughters who can elevate you and dedicate everything for you and give thanks. 
Under the increasing whip, forgetting all the circumstances of your heart that were anxious in the place where tears are connected, we must become those who can praise you on the day of victory that you have longed for, and be able to rejoice with you and comfort you in the victorious 1970s. 
Father, please especially protect this nation. In place of Judaism and the nation of Israel, which could not fulfill their mission for the nation, the lineage of Jesus walked the path of sorrow and despair, the path of the cross, and the path of lamentation that should not have existed. This one nation must unite with countless religious people to establish a victorious Third Israel that aims for the heavenly kingdom of hope. 
The group of unification that knows this tremendous will must be strong and courageous. We must make a new resolution here. We must rediscover a new self here. Therefore, please help us not to lose the dignity we should have as builders of tomorrow, and let us not forget that this is a holy time of connection with your inheritance. 
Father, please protect this time. There are countless children praying towards this place, so please be with them as well. We know that many children of nations are praying towards Korea, which is in a corner of Asia. Therefore, we must feel how fearful this place is. Please protect your children who are calling out to you around the world, shedding tears while longing for their homeland, Korea. There are also your children who are walking the lonely path of pioneers, so please protect them along with the story of being a friend when they were lonely. We earnestly hope and wish that we can become those who testify to the living Father by valuing the grace you have protected us with in the process of pioneering this path that no one knows. 
The group at the headquarters must not incur debt. They must know that they should never become a shameful group that leaves behind disgraceful conditions before those who are devoted. We must realize that we must become those who can protect this place and make it holy. 
Even in the smallest actions, we must be careful not to go against your wishes, and as those who serve you, we must speak words that are respectful. We earnestly request and wish that our entire lives may become lives that can proudly say that we are the beloved sons and daughters who serve you. 
We hope that you will be with us at this time, and we earnestly request that you protect us within your holy will today. We have prayed all these words in the name of the True Parents. Amen. 
<Words> We know that there are many people in this world who believe in Jesus. It is said that there are 3 million believers just in Korea. 
Jesus, who struggled to pioneer a new environment 
Since the will of Jesus is one, those who believe in him must also become one with his will. Furthermore, the country that Jesus desired must also become the country that those who believe in him desire, and the world that Jesus wished for must also become the wish of those who believe in him, which goes without saying. 
Jesus must have had a desired country and world at that time, and he must have had a living environment in which he wanted to live with God. This living environment was certainly not the same as the environment in which Jesus lived for over 30 years in the nation of Israel. 
In other words, Jesus did not just want to live in that environment as it was; he longed for a new environment that could become a foundation of hope by going through that environment. That is why we know that Jesus acted in ways that were contrary to the lifestyle of that time and engaged in missionary activities that were opposite to the prevailing environment in order to pioneer such a living environment. The words of Jesus were not meant to establish a foothold in his fixed social environment. Through the Bible, we can see that Jesus wanted to innovate his environment and establish a living environment that would become the foundation of hope for tomorrow. 
The Bible shows us that Jesus always lived a lonely life. Looking at Jerusalem, he said, “O Jerusalem, Jerusalem, you who kill the prophets and stone those sent to you, how often I have longed to gather your children together, as a hen gathers her chicks under her wings, but you were not willing.” (Luke 13:34) Through these words, we can understand the environment in which Jesus lived at that time. 
The hope of the nation of Israel and the Judaism that worshiped God at that time was to welcome the Messiah. From that standpoint, Judaism and Israel, which should have embraced Jesus as the fruition of their wishes, stood in a position that had nothing to do with Jesus's living environment. 
Therefore, the more miserable the environment became, the more it was not a comfort to Jesus, but rather a heavy burden on the pioneer of tomorrow, Jesus, and it became an environment of internal hardships that required a firm resolution to overcome the difficult circumstances. 
We must understand that Jesus, who was in such a position, could not pray for his own happiness. The environment in which Jesus lived at that time, namely the nation of Israel, which was a vassal of Rome, and Judaism, could not be a foundation of hope for Jesus, nor could it be a foundation of comfort. If he struggled internally and made a resolution, the content of that resolution was how to navigate through the current environment. Jesus wanted to break through the environment of that time and present a new foundation that could be inherited in the future. This is what we can glimpse through the Bible about the life of Jesus at that time. 
From that perspective, we must recognize that Jesus could not help but have feelings of anger and rebellion towards the oppressive Roman regime and the leaders of Judaism, who were sucking the blood of the Israelites and oppressing the Israelite people. Furthermore, he did not have any lingering feelings towards all the patriarchs who ruled over the nation of Judah; rather, he wanted to completely overthrow them at a certain point and prepare a foundation to pass on a new environment to future generations. We can understand through the records of the Scriptures that he made internal resolutions moment by moment to pioneer such a new environment for tomorrow. 
Jesus felt that he had to revolutionize all living environments from the moment he became aware. Since the family centered around his stepfather Joseph and Mary could not become the family that Jesus desired, he could not have a heart of comfort towards his parents in that family. 
Thus, Jesus felt internal hardships from a young age. He could not find comfort through Mary or Joseph, or even through his siblings born to Joseph, nor could he find comfort through all the challenges and living environments he faced. Therefore, no matter how much it was his own family, he felt that he had to break through it and present a new standard of revolution. We must recognize that Jesus felt a sense of responsibility that he could not ignore. 
Personally, it was a family that served his parents, a society he had grown up in since childhood, a church, and the nation of Israel, but for Jesus, the nation of Israel, Judaism, and his family were environments where he could not have a heart of comfort or place his hopes. The more he was pressed into such environments, the more he needed strength, stimulation, and resolution to push through. 
Where to receive this strength, stimulation, and resolution was not a trivial matter. It became a crucial issue for Jesus to maintain the foundation of internal will and strength along with self-awareness. The 30 years of Jesus's life as a carpenter's assistant, although he lived in a humble manner with his mouth shut, was a life of making internal resolutions that no one else knew about. Jesus repeatedly resolved that the nation of Israel should not be such a nation. There was a hidden period of preparation. Furthermore, he felt that he had to confront and fight against the corrupt Judaism, not only in Israel but also in the broader context. 
It was a preparation period where he was earnestly devoted internally, waiting for the right time to come. Moreover, Jesus must have thought that his family would not cooperate, and that the entire ethnic group and nation would oppose him. 
Even as difficulties increased while living as Joseph's assistant, those increasing difficulties did not become a problem for Jesus. For him, the issue was to innovate the nation of Israel and Judaism, to break through all the wrongdoings of the blessed family of Joseph, and to establish a new nation with a new people and create a new world. While longing for such a world in his heart, Jesus endured difficult moments and prepared and resolved to move forward. 
Jesus never forgot his will, even for a moment. While planing, chiseling, or working with tools, he did not think merely about handling a piece of wood. He must have thought that the work he was doing with all the tools was to create the world of hope, the nation of hope, and the church of hope that would be realized on behalf of the nation of Israel. Although the work was merely about carving wood and the environment appeared to be miserable, that work itself was a period of devotion on behalf of the holy nation of Israel and Judaism. 
The 30 years of preparation for Jesus were not a wasted period. It was a period of seriousness more than anyone else could imagine. It was a period of resolution made at the crossroads of sorrow that pierced to the bone, and a period of resolution made while working silently and sweating without being able to express his circumstances before his parents. Every time he faced increasing difficulties, it was a precious period where he discovered that he had to confront those difficulties to pioneer for the nation and the world. 
The environment Jesus was in was not one that could please God, but God could not help but place all future hopes on the internal attitude and the very act of resolution of Jesus. This is Jesus's own position and the environment in which he lived. 
For Jesus, working as a carpenter's assistant was not everything in life. Through that work, he resolved to innovate the nation of Israel and establish the new nation he longed for. Although that resolution was unrelated to carpentry, because he could make internal resolutions through that work, God could view that work with favor. 
From the moment Jesus opened his eyes to the moment he went to bed, he never forgot the nation of Israel and Judaism, nor did he ever stop worrying about the fact that the family of Joseph, representing the Israelite people, was not aligned with his will and was in a position of opposition. He never forgot his will, even for a single hour. 
The countless difficulties that came to Jesus were not difficulties; they became a motivation and stimulation for him to cultivate his strength for the new era in which he had to establish the nation of Israel and innovate Judaism. 
The disciples who did not know Jesus's will 
The disciples who followed Jesus at that time did not understand the serious attitude with which Jesus gathered his disciples to restore the nation of Israel and Judaism. When Peter was mending nets on the boat, Jesus said, “Follow me, and I will make you fishers of men.” (Matthew 4:19) Peter left everything and followed Jesus, but Jesus did not call only Peter as an individual. He called him while longing for Israel, and he called him while recalling Judaism. In other words, the reason he called him was that he wanted to love Judaism and wanted to love the nation of Israel. The purpose of calling him was to leave a legacy for the future, but the very act of calling was motivated by a desire to love Judaism and the nation of Israel, a fact that Peter himself did not know at that time. 
Therefore, the content of what Jesus said was not centered on individual life. The nation I must live in is not such a nation; the nation I must seek is not such a nation.
Jesus thought that the church he was to establish was not the kind of church that was welcomed by the environment of that time. In other words, it was not the Israelite nation that was complacent in the circumstances of that era. Jesus was hoping for a new church and a new Israelite nation.

From that perspective, Jesus educated his disciples. He never forgot that "I am not here for today's Israelite nation, nor for the corrupt Judaism. I did not come as a member of the current church. I am here for the future hoped-for Israelite nation, Judaism, and the lineage of Joseph." 

Jesus spoke from that perspective and tried to make his disciples feel that sentiment. However, the disciples who were with Jesus did not understand this, which led them to continue living in a state of misunderstanding.

The more they longed to love the Israelite nation, the more they vowed to reform Judaism to create an altar that would please the Father. The more they did this, the more anxious Jesus must have felt, incomparable to anyone else. The ignorant disciples of that time did not understand Jesus' deep sorrow.

Even in the Bible, when we look at the dialogues between Jesus and the disciples, we can see that there were many conflicts between the disciples' purposes and living conditions and those of Jesus. For instance, the brothers of John spoke of their desire to achieve success centered around Jesus. How astonished must Jesus have been at that moment? He felt that without blowing up the current position under the banner of revolution, it would be impossible to form the new Israelite nation he desired, and when he looked at those who dreamed of success, how bewildered he must have felt.

The more he looked at such disciples, the more Jesus could not help but feel profound loneliness. Of course, he felt wronged when he suffered in Joseph's household, but when he looked at the disciples, whom he had raised as comrades and sources of comfort to spread the will of hope, he felt even more bewildered. During the three years, Jesus showed them all the examples they needed to follow. How bewildering it was to wash the disciples' feet and encourage them to love one another!

Peter thought of himself in his own way, and the other disciples thought of themselves in their own ways as well. That is why Jesus felt the division among the twelve. He realized that with this state of affairs, he could not establish a new Israelite nation or reform Judaism, and the more he felt this, the more he realized that the people he was dealing with were not objects of comfort but rather subjects of misery.

However, every time Jesus thought, "My love for Peter, James, and others is not as individuals but as a love for the Israelite nation and Judaism," he must have reassured himself countless times. Loving them often meant that they would give him unspeakable blows to his heart. Jesus must have felt a sorrow that no one else could perceive from those ignorant and foolish disciples.

But no matter how much sorrow he felt, he could not vent that frustration on the disciples. Knowing that if he did not suppress that resentment and instead comfort them, he could not even take their current position, how much greater the compounded pain and loneliness Jesus must have felt! We need to think about this again.

Thus, Jesus had to comfort and encourage them. From this perspective, where else could one find someone more pitiful than Jesus? Since he came to maturity, he had harbored a loneliness that he could not express to anyone in order to fulfill his will, and although he devoted himself to teaching the disciples, how often did he feel unspeakable anguish when he saw them repeatedly acting contrary to his heart?

Then how did Jesus overcome such difficulties? He must have thought, "Surely these people, who are to become the future Israelite nation and whom I must love, are better than those who are not." When Jesus shed tears, he must have at least pretended to shed tears with them, and when they crossed the mountain of suffering, he must have tried to follow them. When he showed a lonely expression, he must have tried to comfort them with words. In thinking of such disciples, he must have felt that this was the only path to take. How many prayers must he have offered to God every time he felt this?

Jesus did not love the disciples as individuals but with a heart that embraced the twelve tribes of Israel. Therefore, you must understand that there was a lonely heart intertwined between Jesus and his disciples. While Jesus wanted to go this way, the disciples wanted to go that way. In other words, because what Jesus and the disciples desired conflicted and opposed each other, Jesus constantly thought about how to reconcile this and turn it in the direction he wanted, and how much he must have worried about influencing them through his life. We need to understand this.

In a situation where one cannot even manage their own children, gathering people with no ties or relationships to become disciples and leading them to a place where they could share life and death together, while forming the denomination and nation that God desires, how vast and lonely that road must have been!

However, considering the historical fact that for 4,000 years, God had endured the Israelite people who were to believe in Him, and how much God must have grieved because that Israelite nation betrayed heaven and became unfaithful, we must think about how much Jesus endured, using God's patience until now as a standard. 

Jesus taught the disciples in every possible way so they could understand, hinted at them, and tried to awaken a new will in them through his actions. However, the disciples did not understand Jesus' inner heart. The environment at that time was one of enmity. When the disciples made mistakes, they had to bear the responsibility for the whole, and Jesus, who led the disciples, was trying to create a new relationship in an abnormal environment surrounded by enmity. In this context, Jesus knew that a compounded environment of persecution awaited him. We must understand that Jesus' life was one of unrecognized hardships.

Even in the Bible, when Jesus said, "Woe to you, scribes and Pharisees!" we can see how deeply loneliness and anguish were embedded in his heart. Even the disciples he had gathered during his three years of public ministry could not comfort him in such a heart. Because even the disciples could not be a source of comfort for Jesus, when the time came for him to walk the path of the cross, they all became betrayers.

The disciples whom Jesus loved did not know his circumstances, nor did the parents who loved Jesus understand his situation. Joseph did not know, nor did the lineage centered around Joseph. The Israelite nation and Judaism also did not understand Jesus' circumstances. In such a position, there was not a single person with whom Jesus could share his story.

"I still have much to say to you, but you cannot bear it now." (John 16:21) "If you do not believe when I speak of earthly things, how will you believe when I speak of heavenly things?" (John 3:21) Through these words of Jesus, we can see that he was an unspeakably lonely person.

So who was the one who pushed Jesus into such a place of loneliness? It was undoubtedly the Jews. The lineage representing those Jews, namely the families of Zechariah and Joseph.

When anguish was overwhelming, humanly speaking, feelings of rebellion must have crossed his mind. Feelings of rebellion against the Israelite nation, against the Jews, against the families of Zechariah and Joseph, and even against the three wise men who came to worship him with gold, frankincense, and myrrh when he was born, and against the angels who praised his birth. There were many lonely times when all of this could have become an object of resentment, as we can glean from the biblical context of that time.

That time was not a democratic era like today, where one could freely express their thoughts or form political parties. Therefore, Jesus, who could not speak to anyone and had to silently affirm God's will in his heart, must have felt how miserable it was.

The will that Jesus sought to fulfill could not be accomplished in a day or two. It was not something that could be achieved while eating, drinking, and playing in the corrupted environment of the world. To fulfill that will, he had to discern that environment and create one that would please God, gathering companions in that environment. You must understand that the anguish Jesus faced in such a position was greater than that of any sage in the historical era.

Every time Jesus found himself in such an environment, he thought that the only person God desired was himself, and he felt that God, who had walked the lonely path of pioneering for 4,000 years, was there. He resolved to fulfill the way of filial piety. The more he felt this, the more he could not help but feel profound loneliness.

As resentment toward the world intensified, he felt that he had to fulfill the way of filial piety even more for God. He thought, "Is fulfilling the way of filial piety something I can do alone? Did God send me not to remain as an individual but to fulfill the way of filial piety while leading the Israelite nation and Judaism?" Knowing this, every time Jesus thought of his loneliness before God, he found himself in a position where he could not maintain his dignity before God.

God sent Jesus to unite the Israelite nation and Judaism, to lay the foundation for a new Israelite nation and Judaism, and to march toward a world of one purpose according to Jesus' command. That was God's wish and expectation. Yet, who recognized the lonely heart of Jesus, who stood in a conflicting and isolated position?

Jesus could only draw strength to pioneer this difficult environment from God. Every time he called upon God the Father, he realized that he was a person who had no face before God and was unable to take responsibility for the world. You must understand that Jesus had to continue living a life where he shed sad tears that no one else knew about.

Every time Jesus welcomed a new morning, he hoped that although he had been in a lonely position yesterday, today would bring about new events, and he would find someone who could be a companion on the path he had to take and a model on the road he had to pioneer. However, the foolish disciples, who did not know Jesus' dire circumstances, could not become such people. Therefore, Jesus must have been bewildered. When they were hungry, they complained about being hungry in the desert or anywhere else, and when they were thirsty, they complained about being thirsty, and when their clothes were shabby, they complained about that too. How many times did they complain like this during the three years they followed Jesus? Every time Jesus witnessed this, he must have been bewildered. The people of that time sent Jesus, who had come to this earth as the Prince of God, away in such loneliness. You must understand that this was the path of Jesus.

Because Jesus was one who bore a will, he was lonely because of that will, he shed tears because of that will, and he was prepared to face death because of that will. We must understand that Jesus had to reject his parents and treat his brothers as enemies because of that will. What was the sad circumstance that forced Jesus to say to his beloved mother Mary, "Woman, what does that have to do with me?" (John 2:4)?

Jesus' stepfather Joseph abandoned Jesus' hopes and expectations. Jesus' siblings also mocked him, saying, "If you want to be known to the world, you should go up to Jerusalem for the Feast of Tabernacles. Why aren't you going?" The fact that even his siblings mocked him indicates that Joseph's family failed in their responsibilities and that Mary also failed in hers.

Jesus was lonely, having to betray the parents he should love and stand in the position of an enemy, and he could not help but rebuke the scribes and Pharisees who led Judaism, saying, "Woe to you, scribes and Pharisees!" What caused Jesus to change from a position of love to one of rebuke? It was because of the will. Because Jesus understood the will, and because he had to follow that path of will, he could not help but rebel against the Israelite nation and Judaism.

Regarding the Israelite nation that should be loved, and the Jerusalem that represented that nation, the center of all religious authority and sovereignty, Jesus had to utter a curse, saying, "O Jerusalem, Jerusalem! Do you wish to reach heaven? Beware of falling into the abyss!" Who understood the pitiful and sorrowful circumstances of Jesus? This was more painful than death and more difficult than dying, yet who understood the will that Jesus harbored, and who understood the story of Jesus?

So why was Jesus branded a traitor to his nation? It was because of the will. If Jesus had not known God's will, there would have been no mention of the suffering of the cross. If there had been no will of God, he would not have stood in a position where he could not receive love from his father and mother, nor would he have endured the humiliation of being accused of being possessed by Beelzebub by his relatives.

Why was he pushed into such a miserable and painful position? It was because he knew God's will and harbored that will. That will was one that could not be exchanged even for the Israelite nation, one that could not be exchanged even for Judaism, and one that could not be exchanged even for beloved parents. It was a will that could not be exchanged even for his relatives or the world of that time, so Jesus always longed to become the victorious self who fulfilled that will.

From this perspective, the statement that there is no righteous person, not even one, was made centering on Jesus himself. From the perspective of the will, Jesus could not be considered righteous. From the perspective of the will, he was a lonely person. He was someone who could resent and curse this earth.

Therefore, we must reflect on the Bible centered on the will and today...
We must look at Christianity again. The will of Jesus is not two; it is one. Jesus was driven by that will alone, always lonely, and walked the path of death while shedding blood on the cross. He left behind the promise of His return while walking that path of death centered on the will. If there were no will of God, then all these events would have no relation to Jesus at all. So where does that will remain, and where should it be reaped? It must remain through Christianity and be reaped through Christianity. This is the problem.

Then, can we find the will that Jesus cried out for and sought after among Christians who believe in Him today? Has today’s Christianity become like the Judaism that Jesus envisioned? It has not. Do today’s Christians possess the nation of Israel that Jesus was looking for? They do not. Do they have the kind of family that Jesus longed for? They do not. When asked if they have the relationships of husband and wife, parents, and the bonds of bride and groom that Jesus wanted to bless, the answer is no. Do they have the brothers and sisters that Jesus wanted to love? The answer is no. Do they have parents whom Jesus could not help but love? The answer is also no.

Given the current position of Christianity, what should the Unification Church do today? We must have brothers and families that can love along with the will that Jesus cherished, we must have tribes that can love, churches that can love, and nations that can love. In other words, we should not have the Israel, church, and family that made Jesus lament, but we must have a nation, church, and family that can make Jesus rejoice, centered on His will. Only then can we bear the fruit of the will that Jesus desired today.

In this way, I want to ask whether Christianity, which is in a position to pursue such a goal, has the mindset to do so today. Isn’t that the heart of God and Jesus?

Therefore, you must be able to serve Jesus, transcending the sins of the Israelite people who drove Him to the path of death on the cross. Furthermore, that must be our wish. Thus, we must come before Jesus and say, "Isn’t this the family you were looking for? Isn’t this the church you were seeking? Isn’t this the nation you wanted to love? I offer all of this to you, please accept it."

One person who can do this is more precious than millions who claim to believe in Jesus. It is not the number of believers that matters, but the individual who bears fruit. However, among the countless Christians until now, there has been no such person.

We must understand what the will of God and Jesus is. Today, the wish of Christians who simply believe in the Bible is to go to heaven. Was Jesus’ wish, "Father, I will believe in you and go to heaven"? Was that His wish? Jesus’ wish was to send those who wished to go to heaven to heaven. His desire was to hold onto the poor souls who were destined for hell and send them to heaven. Even if He had to go to hell or walk the path of death, His wish was to send humanity to heaven. Isn’t saving humanity the wish of Jesus? Without going through that path, the nation and church that Jesus envisioned will not emerge.

We must take this opportunity to clarify the essence of faith and analyze how traditional Christian thought has become divided. In other words, among today’s Christians, how many believers can be a source of comfort before Jesus, surpassing the apostles who followed Him and the people and Jewish law scholars who rejected Him?

Then, does the will of Jesus remain in today’s Christianity? Those who claim to believe in Jesus today say, "Oh! Lord, come!" "Bridegroom Lord, please come to me!" But if He actually comes, what will they do? He is returning because the will was not fulfilled at that time; is today’s environment and living situation one where the returning Lord can rejoice? Have they prepared to receive Jesus? Am I looking at Jesus through the will of God, or am I trying to receive Jesus through myself? Am I trying to serve God as my tool, or am I trying to become God’s tool? That is the question.

Therefore, today, we Unification Church members must understand the circumstances of Jesus who bore the will. We must understand that "Jesus would have wanted to love Israel like this. He would have wanted to love Judaism like this. He would have wanted to love His family and tribe like this." The wish of Jesus is to unite even His father and mother to love Judaism and the nation of Israel. It is not, "I will be a son who knows only my father and mother." Even if it means abandoning His family, Jesus’ wish was to save the nation of Israel and Judaism. Shouldn’t it be so?

Is Jesus’ will that we live as we please, neglecting God’s will, and just be filial to our parents? Jesus had the will to abandon His living environment and establish a new nation from that place, so He could not help but clash with all of His living circumstances. Jesus did not intend to just find a house, repair it, and live there; He wanted to tear everything down and build a new house. That is why He said, "A man’s enemies will be those of his own household." (Matt 10:36) From the perspective of family, parents may be enemies; from the perspective of the nation, the sovereign of that nation may be an enemy; and from the perspective of the church, the law scholars may be enemies. In other words, enemies can be husbands, sovereigns, and church leaders. This is the path we must take.

Looking at the Unification Church members, who are the enemies? If a wife believes in the Unification Church, her husband becomes an enemy; if a husband believes in the Unification Church, his wife becomes an enemy. Then the nation becomes an enemy, and the established church becomes an enemy. If we do not stand in a position where these three parts can become enemies, the path of joy will not emerge. We reap what we sow. Since Jesus sowed in such a way, we must also reap in such a position.

In that sense, the Unification Church has passed the test. How much opposition did husbands show when their wives attended the Unification Church? The teacher has seen all kinds of things. Did their heads not get broken? Did their legs not get broken? Did their faces not get bruised? Did their clothes not get torn? The teacher has seen all sorts of things. Even so, when they come to church and tell the teacher their circumstances, can the teacher curse them? Such experiences are part of the path of the will. Because Jesus walked such a path, we also face such situations. It is a destiny that cannot be avoided, and as we bear the responsibility to resolve the events that unfolded centered on Jesus, now the Unification Church is also gaining a good reputation.

The more families oppose, the more nations oppose, and the more churches oppose, what stands out is the will of Jesus, the will of Jesus. Even if we lose the nation, we must say, "The will of Jesus!" Even if we lose the church, we must say, "The will of Jesus!" Even if we lose our parents and the entire family, we must say, "The will of Jesus!" It is through the conclusion of the will of Jesus that we can find the foundation of the lost family again and regain the lost church. Furthermore, we can establish new connections with the nation and start anew. That is why God places us in such a position. Therefore, unless you stand in such a position, you cannot walk the path of the will.

Thus, we Unification Church members must voluntarily walk that path. We must choose to go rather than being driven by God. Jesus was saddened because His disciples could not take responsibility, so we must choose to take responsibility. By voluntarily leaving our families, voluntarily leaving the church, and voluntarily distancing ourselves from the nation, we become the frontline in the battle for the will. This is not for the sake of the current nation, church, or family, but for the sake of a new nation, a new church, and a new family.

Therefore, if you spend your life standing in such a position, you will come to know the circumstances of Jesus who bore the will. However, to stand in such a position, today’s church cannot suffice. The faith I have believed until now cannot suffice. There must be a movement to love the village centered on the will, to organize a new church centered on the will, and to gather new disciples centered on the will. Only then will you come to know the circumstances of Jesus well.

For example, just as one must give birth to and raise a child to feel the heart of a parent, one must experience rejection from other churches, rejection from parents, and persecution from the nation to truly realize, "Ah, this is the loneliness of Jesus."

The history of suffering and persecution that the Unification Church has gone through for decades has not been to destroy the Unification Church. Of course, during that period, there may have been a negative balance, but you must understand that it is an essential suffering and persecution that cannot be overlooked in establishing a normal tradition.

How much have you shed tears centered on the will? That is the condition to come closer to Jesus. Just as all the disciples who believed and followed Jesus fled when He was about to die on the cross, if those who were evangelized through you abandon the will and leave in a day or two, you will feel a heartache that pierces to your bones. When you feel that, tears will flow uncontrollably.

Isn’t that strange? Why do tears come out when they have nothing to do with you? It is because you are centered on the will. You are holding onto them and pleading with them. Just as you would be filial to your parents, you would plead with them to walk this path together, as you would serve God and the nation. It is similar to seeking forgiveness from an enemy; with that heart, you hold onto that one person and plead with them. At such times, you will come to understand the circumstances of Jesus, who had to seek out His disciples for forty days after the resurrection.

A parent who has raised many children cannot have an evil heart. From this perspective, we can discover the emotional story that we cannot leave God even if we die in such a position.

We must advance to a position beyond Jesus. Jesus Himself has gone, but the will of God has not gone. As history flows, that will will come to fruition. We must face that will. However, you must not face that will with your own will. You must establish and fulfill the will of Jesus as it is. You must become the representative of Jesus.

Today, in Christianity, there are those who say "Moon Jesus" regarding the teacher of the Unification Church, but you must all become Jesus. Jesus is the seed. Just as a seed bears fruit when sown, you must become the fruit harvested from the seed of Jesus. If you believe in Jesus, it must be so. However, you must not become the Jesus who was rejected before the old Judaism. From the position of the rejected Jesus, we must advance to a position where we are welcomed. Jesus left in sorrow, but we must go in joy. In terms of the results of the will, we must see what Jesus could not see. In that sense, we are better than Jesus.

Now is the age of democracy. So, is there anyone who opposes the establishment of the Unification Church? Is there anyone who threatens my life if I go out and evangelize? Looking at this environment, we are in a better age than the time when Jesus preached the gospel. We are living in a time far better than that of Jesus. Those of us who are receiving such benefits of the times must surely resolve the emotional burdens we carry. You must inherit the will that Jesus cherished.

Jesus, in the position of an older brother or a father, cherished that will, so you must inherit the will of Jesus. Jesus is like a parent. He is also the representative of the brothers, the representative of the family, and the representative of the nation. Ultimately, He is the one who possesses all the qualities that humanity must have, so we must inherit His will as it is. Without inheriting that, we cannot be heirs in that nation.

Therefore, you must once again imagine the pitiful scene of Jesus carrying the cross and walking the path of the will through His 30 years of private life and 3 years of public life.

How long did Jesus wait for the day when He could love the nation of Israel, which He could not love at that time? How long did He wait to realize that love for the church, which He could not love? How long did He wait for the day when He could live loving His brothers? However, we have the heart to love our brothers, the heart to love the church, and the heart to love the nation that Jesus longed for, and we have a church that can love without hesitation, and we have brothers who bear the name of Unification Church members. In that sense, the Unification Church stands in a position to love more than anyone in the Republic of Korea.

In other words, we are in an amazing position to establish a new Third Israel church that can inherit the Third Israel nation, and we are standing in that position. Therefore, now is the time to put forth our utmost sincerity. This can be understood by looking at everything. Therefore, if you miss this time, it will be difficult to have such a time again.

Those who have not crossed the 38th parallel do not know what the 38th parallel is like. Therefore, we must understand that we are in this moment and must intertwine the family environment, tribal environment, church environment, and national environment that can restore and return centered on the will that Jesus cherished. In other words, you must be those who resolve the present well with the joy of fulfilling what Jesus longed for and inherit the will of Jesus.

<Prayer> Loving Father, we must understand that even in the moment we think we will not die, death can come upon us. We know that those who say they will die do not die. Therefore, even if death comes upon us in the moment we think we will not die, we must not be flustered. Jesus went up to the Garden of Gethsemane and said, "Abba Father, all things are possible for You; take this cup away from Me; nevertheless, not what I will, but what You will." (Mark 14:36)
We understand that there was a distance between Your will and the will of the Father. While Jesus looked at the family and the disciples, His will was to look at the world and the realm of Israel, and we know that there was a distance here. 

Living should not be for the suffering self of the present, but should be for the future of the nation of Israel and the world. We know that Jesus, who understood this, went up to the Garden of Gethsemane and prayed such a prayer. 

Father, the children of unity gathered here have also entered onto a similar path of destiny, so may it not be according to our will, but according to Your will. May it not be according to the will of the Unification Church, but according to Your will. We understand that if we make a mistake, there may be a will of the Unification Church, so please do not let there be a will of the Unification Church. The Unification Church must be one that follows primarily Your will. We know that without standing in such a position, the Unification Church will drift away. 

Father, please remember Your children gathered here. Currently, we are thinking about the mainstream and the non-mainstream. Therefore, the question of which path I should take becomes an issue. Father, I know well that You have held onto and fought for this denomination for decades. I have overcome to this day because I realized that the only way to relieve Your loneliness in every scene where I shed tears is through this path. 

Father, please love the Republic of Korea. The day when we can embrace the five provinces in the North in Your bosom must come soon. I know that the new way of unification will not come through the hands of any politician today. I understand that it can only be achieved through Your love and Your hands. We know that when we can embody the victorious sons and daughters who can love beyond the North and South, unification will be realized. 

Father, the history of the separation of Cain and Abel has manifested today as the fate of being divided into North and South centered on the Republic of Korea. The tragic history of the separation of the nation of Israel and Judaism has been re-enacted today in the Republic of Korea. Centered on Panmunjom, which encompasses a global platform, we are divided into the democratic world and the communist world. We understand that today’s Panmunjom is where Satan negotiates with God and presents conditions for accusation, drawing a line of global good. 

In light of this issue, the Republic of Korea must rise up from this earth as Apollo 11 did, using this earth as a base to soar and become the founder of a new world and the leader of a new history. Although this nation does not know the mission it has, the insignificant group of unification knows it well. 

Now we must solemnly bow before Your holy image and call upon You in a true sense after knowing You. We must call upon the name of the true Father. And we must become true filial sons and daughters who can resonate with Your heart. We do not wish to be adopted sons and daughters. We hope to stand in Your direct dominion, where we can deeply feel Your sorrowful heart. 

To become such sons and daughters, we have forsaken our families, forsaken the church, and forsaken our nation, coming forth with nothing in empty hands, holding only Your will. Because we have embraced Your will, we have come to understand that in heaven there are individuals, families, tribes, nations, and the world. We are in the process of hoping to become the subjects of a new individual, a new family, a new tribe, a new nation, and a new world that can be shaped by our oneness with You. 

Father, please help these to firmly maintain the position they stand in. They must understand that they should not be dominated by their circumstances, but must have the subjectivity to dominate those circumstances. We have come to know that this is precisely the group of unification that must advance centered on the new will. 

To do this, as people who embrace Your will, both men and women must stand strong and courageous, centered on the new spirit of the nation, and must have autonomy. Furthermore, they must possess the ability to be pioneers and become the soldiers on the front lines. Let us be Your sons and daughters who resolve to do this. We must not be like the twelve apostles who fled, but must become those who are willing to take arrows for Jesus and bear swords in His place, fulfilling our responsibilities. We must become Your sons and daughters who can love our nation and our church with such integrity and resolve. 

We have a historical and sacred connection to love not only this age but also the future descendants, so we must become Your sons and daughters who fight to solidify this foundation. 

Now we have entered the last critical juncture of the 1970s. During the remaining time, what shall we hope for? We must repent for being unfaithful to the will, repent for centering ourselves and accepting the will, and lament and repent for having used and trampled upon You for our own benefit. Thus, we must fulfill the duty of devotion to welcome the historical year of 1971 with a new heart, dedicating this year as a year of joy to bring glory before You. 

We know that we are the group of unification who must praise Your glory and shed tears of joy by sacrificing on behalf of all people. 

Father, there must be a day of freedom and liberation for those who are experiencing the sorrowful and heart-wrenching days. There must be a day when we can shed tears of gratitude, proclaiming that the day our Father desired has come in a free form. That day must be the day of unification of the nation and the day we can affirm the glory of victory, so we must understand that until that time comes, we cannot take off the cross. We must also understand that without this, this nation cannot become the foundation for the restoration of the world. 

We understand the teachings of the principle that we must establish the nation of Adam. Therefore, we hope to become the group of unification that can be the founder of Israel, with all our strength and single-hearted devotion, so that we can be the ones who can disappear. We have fought with this heart until now. If there is any merit in this, it is only Yours, and if there is anything to boast of, it is only You. 

However, since there is still a path to go, we must drag our weary legs and go on, and even while managing our tired bodies, we must maintain the position of priests. When we forget this, please discipline us even if You must use a whip. 

Please do not allow us to be a group that receives the gifts from You in a filthy manner regarding the hopes of the nation and the world. We must create a holy altar of victory where the heart of heaven and the heart of the earth can connect, and where the heart of the Father and the heart of the children can connect, so we earnestly hope that You will preside over this. 

Even if we are few in number, we must first become Your true sons and daughters. Please protect Your families scattered throughout the world. Have compassion on those who are being criticized in their circumstances and environments, and lead them personally. We earnestly hope that we can become a group that can walk directly along the path of heaven that You desire. 

Without loving the nation, we cannot love the family, and without finding the nation, we cannot love the church. This fate lies before us, and we must fulfill this to say that we have performed our duty of loyalty and our duty of filial piety. Knowing this, we must resolutely pledge to walk that path, embodying the image of a heavenly hero and not delaying the mission of a pioneer. 

Today is a holy day, and there are those who pray and gather their hearts for this place, so may Your mercy be upon their hearts that are concerned for Your will, and may the heart of compassion be with them. We thank You for being with us at this time, and we pray all these words in the name of the True Parents. Amen.
